Current Affairs Commentary

Popular Morale Amid National Crisis 21

Last year, at the outset of the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, students and youths across the country were stirred and expressed their determination to defend the nation and resist aggression, even at the cost of their lives. We were deeply gratified, believing that external threats had awakened our seemingly listless nation, injecting it with vitality. With such morale and vigor, China would not perish. However, with the renewed fall of Yu Pass and the emergency in North China, the news we received was not of students and youths in Peiping and Tientsin uniting to prepare for resisting the invaders, but rather of "early vacations" and "ice-skating entertainment," a series of bizarre occurrences. As the national crisis deepens and the nation teeters on the brink of collapse, now is precisely the time for our people to endure hardship, steel themselves, and prepare to make sacrifices. Yet, students and youths, who are the backbone of society and the future masters of the country, are either seeking entertainment or evading danger for personal comfort, fully revealing a cowardly and complacent mentality. The aggressors are not to be feared, nor even the fall of the nation; what is truly to be feared is this cowardly and complacent mentality, like swallows building nests on curtains, unaware of the impending danger, or fish lying on a chopping board, awaiting slaughter with eyes closed. This is the incurable disease that will lead to the demise of our nation. Faced with enormous difficulties, they remain unmoved. As the aggressors enter the country, they only know to flee death. Those who used to criticize others are now following the same path. Those students who are ice-skating and fleeing death, try to reflect in silence, can you truly feel no shame in your hearts? However, we do not wish to place blame solely on the students. Since the outbreak of the September 18th Incident, which has lasted for over a year, the authorities in charge have never failed to declare their determination and preparedness to resist aggression to our people. Yet, in reality, the situation remains one of no fighting and no retreat. Moreover, factions within the party are divided, and warlords continue to engage in endless conflicts. The government has failed to demonstrate to the people a firm attitude, clear facts, and a unified goal, to rally the divided national spirit, establish a central belief, and concentrate the scattered forces, so that popular morale can be strengthened and the people's spirit can be anchored. Instead, they procrastinate and wait, hoping to seize opportunities to die for the country. As a result, the surging popular morale weakens and then disappears. The timid sink into complacency, while the audacious take risks for their own gratification. Thus, it is inevitable that some students in Peiping and Tientsin are either enjoying themselves ice-skating or fleeing for safety, while others are resorting to radical actions such as throwing bombs and sending warning letters. Therefore, it would be unfair to solely blame the students and youths for the decline in popular morale today.

Japanese Troops Temporarily Halt Advance in Nanling 22

Volunteer Army in Kailu Continues Fierce Fighting with Japanese Troops

Enemy Establishes General Transportation Station in Jinzhou

(Peiping) This morning's telegram from Chengde reported that after Japanese troops in Nanling provoked an incident, they were repelled by our forces and dared not advance further. Japanese armored vehicles remain in Chaoyang Temple. Local militias have united with the stationed troops to jointly resist foreign aggression. (20th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Beizhangyingzi, 35 li from Suizhong, is occupied by Japanese troops. Residents, filled with anger, have fled into the mountains, filling up the village wells. Lacking water, the Japanese troops are retreating towards Suizhong. The volunteer army in Kailu is engaged in fierce fighting with enemy cavalry in Shuli. The Japanese barracks in Guitai have been burned down, and the Japanese troops have suffered heavy casualties. (20th Dispatch)

=Tang Yulin Goes to the Front Lines for Inspection=

(Tientsin) Tang Yulin departed from Chengde on the 20th morning to inspect the front lines and encourage the soldiers to defend their territory and resist aggression. The enemy is digging trenches and setting up electric fences in Chaoyang Temple, Beipiao, Nanling, and other places, seemingly aware that attacking along this route is difficult and planning to choose another route to attack Rehe and Xin'an. (20th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Tang Yulin was originally scheduled to go to the front lines for inspection this morning. A telegram received from Chengde this afternoon stated that Tang postponed his departure to wait for Tang Zuo's return to Rehe to discuss financial matters. (20th Dispatch)

=Heavy Fighting in the Kailu Area=

(Peiping) Captain Cui of Kailu County reported that the volunteer armies of Feng Zhanhai and Li Haiqing are engaged in heavy fighting with Japanese troops in Kailu. It is rumored that a portion of the Japanese Kwantung Army's 6th Division is retreating. Recently, about 500 Japanese troops were transferred from Liaoning. (20th Dispatch)

(Peiping) Tang Zuo arrived in Rehe this afternoon. A telegram to Peiping this evening stated that Rehe Province is calm. Except for Chaoyang, Kailu, and Lingnan counties, which are slightly tense, the other counties are generally safe. The volunteer army in Kailu is still engaged in daily fighting with Japanese troops. (20th Dispatch)

=National Salvation Army Attacks Enemy Rear=

(Peiping) On the 16th, Wang Yongliang, commander of the 2nd Brigade of the National Salvation Army, sent Chief of Staff Lin Chengyan to lead the 2nd and 3rd Regiments to attack the enemy's rear in Shahe and Yangshuwazi. After two days and nights of fierce fighting, the enemy suffered heavy casualties. We captured dozens of enemy rifles and a large quantity of military supplies. Due to the arrival of enemy reinforcements and the bombing by airplanes, our army temporarily retreated to Lingnan for replenishment. Wang's troops are currently in contact with the troops of Feng Zhanhai and Liu Guitang, taking responsibility for the southern route of Tongliao and determined to launch a full-scale attack. They are currently preparing food supplies. (20th Dispatch)

=Japanese Troops Establish General Station in Jinzhou=

(Peiping) On the morning of the 19th, two more Japanese transport ships arrived in Huludao, fully loaded with supplies and ammunition. They have been unloaded and transported to Jinzhou. The enemy has established a general transportation station in Jinzhou. (20th Dispatch)

=Japanese Troops Telegraph Home Requesting Reinforcements=

(Peiping) The Japanese military is still actively deploying troops for military operations in Rehe. Due to the length of the battle line and the insufficient number of troops, they have telegraphed home requesting reinforcements of four divisions. The Japanese military is concerned about international attention and has not yet approved the request. They plan to change their approach by massively arming immigrants and first transferring a division from the Northeast to Korea. The 19th Division is already in the process of deployment. (20th Dispatch)

=Japanese Side Transfers Bandit Troops as Vanguard=

(Peiping) The Japanese side feels that the gathering of volunteer armies along the border of Rehe is a thorny military issue. In order to avoid Japanese casualties, they have decided to transfer Yu Zhishan, Zhang Haipeng, and Cheng Guorui as the vanguard. To prevent each unit from turning against them, they are ordering mixed operations to mutually restrain each other. At the same time, they are using Mongol bandits to harass the area. Currently, there are 600 Japanese troops, 2,000 bandit troops, and more than 5,000 Mongol bandits stationed in the Tongliao area. (20th Dispatch)

=He Sui Goes from Chaoyang to Lingnan=

(Peiping) National Government representative He Sui has arrived in Chaoyang, distributed the military expenses for Dong's troops, and transferred to Lingnan. There were no major conflicts on the front lines yesterday. (20th Dispatch)

=Large Number of Japanese Troops Transferred to Suizhong=

(Peiping) On the 18th, Captain Dong of Chaoyang sent Jin, a staff officer from the brigade headquarters, to Rehe to report to Tang that Japanese troops have recently built strong fortifications in Chaoyang Temple and Nanling, and are forcibly conscripting laborers. Trains on the Jin-Chao Road are running non-stop day and night. Large numbers of Japanese troops have been transferred to Suizhong County. Japanese troops are posting sentries and trains traveling to Suizhong are closing and dimming their lights to prevent our side from spying on Japanese military movements. (20th Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Japanese army has been continuously transferring troops to western Liaoning. The Mogi cavalry and Kuroda infantry brigades stationed in Heilongjiang have been completely transferred to Suizhong and Jin County. The main force that had been fighting the volunteer army in the Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces has been transported via the Tao'ang Road to Tongliao Qianjiadian. (20th Dispatch)

=Rehe Garrison Receives Back Pay=

(Peiping) The Rehe garrison has received four months of back pay, all in silver dollars. Various parties are flocking to Rehe to offer their condolences, greatly boosting morale. (20th Dispatch)

=National Salvation Army Decides to Launch a Three-Pronged Counterattack=

(Peiping) Wang Delin of the Jilin National Salvation Army and Deputy Commanders Kong Xianrong, Wu Yicheng, and Wang Yuzhen have held discussions and decided to launch a three-pronged counterattack. Kong Xianrong will be responsible for the central assault, Wang Yuzhen for the left flank, and Wu Yicheng for the right flank. Wang will supervise the army from the rear. It is expected that the war in the eastern sector will break out soon. (20th Dispatch)

Hulunbuir Entirely Under Japanese Control 23

(Peiping) The entire territory of Hulunbuir is currently entirely under the jurisdiction of the Japanese in terms of civil and military affairs. According to reliable foreign sources in Harbin today, the Mongol princes are now acquiescing to this situation. (20th Reuters dispatch)

Guangdong Assembles People's Volunteer Army, Prepares to Go North Empty-Handed to Resist Aggression 24

Selecting Two Elite and Robust Regiments from the Army

Weapons to be Issued by the Central Government

(Hong Kong) With 12 million in military arrears in Guangdong, Chen Jitang has decided to implement downsizing two months ahead of schedule. The original plan was to eliminate the weak and retain the strong, but now the plan has changed to select two elite and robust regiments to form a Guangdong People's Volunteer Army to go north empty-handed to resist aggression. Weapons will be provided by the central government. Chen has telegraphed to summon the generals at the front to return to the province to discuss the issue of suppressing bandits and the survival of the Third Army. Yu Hanmou, Wang Zanbin, and others will arrive soon. (20th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) The Political Council sent Chen Rong to Hong Kong on the 20th to meet with Hu Hanmin to discuss the current situation. It is rumored that Chen Mingshu is about to return to the country. (20th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Zou Lu said on the 20th that he had received news from Nanjing that the central government had made full preparations to resist aggression, but whether this is true remains to be proven by future events. (20th Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Li Zongren is scheduled to go to the province on the evening of the 20th. It is rumored that Huang Shaoxiong will accompany him. (20th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Guangdong People's Assistance to the Northeast Volunteer Army Fund sent a telegram to He Zhuguo and Shi Shi'an stating that since the Japanese have occupied Yu Pass, they still hope that they will fight to the end. They have remitted 5,000 yuan through the Bank of China to help with military expenses and express their slight intentions. (20th Dispatch)

Zheng Xiaoxu Shot, Severely Wounded 25

The Assailant, a Korean, Has Been Arrested

(Peiping) According to a certain source, Zheng Xiaoxu was assassinated on the 12th. Zheng did not die, but was only wounded in the abdomen, and the injury was very serious. The driver, Mr. Sheng, was shot and killed at the time. The rumor that Zheng died was a misunderstanding of the news of the driver's death. The assailant was a member of a Korean independence party and has been arrested. He is currently being interrogated by the Japanese Military Police Headquarters in Changchun. The weapon was a pistol, not a bomb. His target was General Mutō, but he mistakenly hit Zheng's car. There is a rumor that Mutō suffered minor injuries. (20th Dispatch)

Su Bingwen and Others Arrive in Vladivostok 26

According to information received from a certain place in Tsuruga, Su Bingwen and his party of forty people, who arrived in Vladivostok on the 18th, are now awaiting a convenient ship to Shanghai. (20th Dentsu dispatch)

(Peiping) After Su Bingwen entered Russia, a unit of his subordinates, more than 5,000 people, hid in Mopanshan, Jiang Province. The Japanese army suspected them of being bandits and sent more than 400 troops to suppress them on the 14th of this month, but they were all annihilated by Su's troops. (19th Dispatch)

Mutō Convenes Important Military Conference 27

(Peiping) Mutō, the Japanese ambassador stationed in the puppet state, sent secret telegrams to Japanese military spies in North China and the Northeast a few days ago, setting a date for a military conference to be held in Lushun. The main idea of the original telegram was that with the national crisis at hand, it is time for the regeneration of our nation and the beginning of a new country, and that matters urgently need to be discussed with the generals. It was specifically stated that a crucial military leaders' conference would be held on January 23 at the headquarters of the Kwantung Army Fortress in Lushun. It was signed by Mutō Nobuyoshi himself. (20th Dispatch)

Legislative Yuan Holds First General Assembly Yesterday 28

=Draft Cooperative Law Referred for Review Again=

=Announces List of Various Legal and Regulatory Committees=

Constitutional Drafting Conference to be Held

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its third first general assembly at 9:00 a.m. on the 20th. Sixty-five members, including Zhu Hezhong, attended. Sun Ke, the President of the Yuan, presided, and Liang Hancao served as the Secretary-General. The following items were discussed: (1) The report by the Economic Committee of the Yuan, in conjunction with Committee Member Lou Tongsun, on the draft Cooperative Law. Resolution: To be referred to Jiao Yitang, Shi Shangkuan, Dai Xiujun, Huang Youchang, Lou Tongsun, Ma Yinchu, Feng Zhaoyi, Chen Changheng, Wei Tingsheng, Tang Youren, Wu Shangying, Ma Chaojun, Zhang Zhihan, Chen Zhaoying, Wang Qi, and fifteen other committee members for review, convened by Committee Member Jiao Yitang. (20th Central News Agency dispatch)

(Nanjing) At the general assembly of the Legislative Yuan on the 20th, Sun Ke announced the list of various legal and regulatory committees. The word "drafting" was removed from the names of each committee. Each committee will be composed of five members, except for the Constitution Drafting Committee, which is particularly important and will have thirty-six members. Sun will serve concurrently as the Chairman, with Zhang Zhiben and Wu Jingxiong as Vice-Chairmen. The Civil Law Committee will be convened by Fu Bingchang, with Lin Bin and others as members; the Criminal Law Committee will be convened by Liu Kejian, with Luo Ding and others as members; the Commercial Law Committee will be convened by Ma Yinchu, with Wei Tingsheng and others as members; the Labor Law Committee will be convened by Shi Weihuan, with Ma Chaojun and others as members; the Self-Government Law Committee will be convened by Huang Youchang, with Zhang Zhiben and others as members; and the Land Law Committee will be convened by Wu Shangying, with Chen Changheng and others as members. (20th Central News Agency dispatch)

(Nanjing) Sun Ke believes that the drafting of the constitution must be carried out actively and has decided to convene the first constitution drafting conference next week. He has already telegraphed Vice-Chairmen Zhang Zhiben and Wu Jingxiong, urging them to come to Nanjing to work as soon as possible. (20th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) On the 20th, the Legislative Yuan passed a resolution to establish a Constitution Drafting Committee, appointing Zhou Yizhi, Dong Qizheng, Jiao Yitang, Chen Zhaoying, Ding Chaowu, Fu Rulin, Huang Youchang, Liu Guanxun, Lü Zhiyi, Xu Yuangao, Feng Ziyou, Ma Chaojun, Fu Bingchang, Deng Zhaoyin, Wu Shangying, Shi Shangkuan, Lin Bin, Dai Xiujun, Lou Tongsun, Huang Jilu, Liu Kejian, Shi Weihuan, Luo Ding, Cheng Zhonghang, Di Ying, Sheng Zhenwei, Qu Cengze, Zhao Chen, Wang Kunlun, Deng Gongxuan, Zhong Tianxin, Yang Gongda, Tao Xuan, Wang Xiaoying, Ma Yinchu, Chen Ruxuan, and thirty-six others as members. Zhang Zhiben and Wu Jingxiong were appointed as Vice-Chairmen, and President Sun served concurrently as Chairman. (20th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Sun Ke, Liang Hancao, Fu Bingchang, and others went to Shanghai at 3:00 p.m. on the 20th and are scheduled to return to Nanjing on the 23rd. (20th Central News Agency dispatch)

Japanese Goods Still Flood Market Amid Boycott 29

Japanese Side Implements Dumping Policy

(Nanjing) Business sources report that after the sharp depreciation of the Japanese currency, the cost of Japanese goods has decreased, and Japan is now implementing a dumping policy in China. Tens of thousands of tons of goods have arrived in China one after another. In the past two months, businesses have outwardly expressed their refusal to sell inferior goods due to the warnings of patriotic groups, but in reality, they are secretly accepting them, and the amount is no less than before. Goods such as cotton textiles, hardware, seafood, stationery, and coal are still being imported in large quantities every month, using both dumping and distribution methods. In the past two months, the amount has consistently been over ten million tons. Taking electric light bulbs as an example, Japan is implementing a dumping policy in China. Recent investigations have revealed that approximately 600,000 light bulbs are being dumped in Shanghai, Hankou, and North China each month, with each bulb selling for only seven to nine cents. This price is two-thirds to three-quarters lower than other foreign goods and one-half to two-thirds lower than domestic goods. Recently, they have also been imitating the products of Western merchants, causing domestic goods to be hit hard, and their sales are almost completely replaced. (20th Dispatch)

Tariff Law to be Finalized Soon 30

Resumption of the Japanese Parliament

The Saito Cabinet in a Difficult Situation 77

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 20th: The parliament is scheduled to reconvene on the 21st. The Saito Cabinet, facing unprecedented internal and external difficulties centered on the Manchurian issue, is being ignored by the Seiyukai. Even the Minseito, which considers itself a party in alliance with the government, has recently shown signs of changing direction. National unity exists only in name. Therefore, the trend after the resumption of parliament is highly noteworthy. At the beginning of the session, Prime Minister Saito will deliver a speech on policy direction, Foreign Minister Uchida will speak on diplomacy, and Finance Minister Takahashi will speak on finance. Then, a questioning battle will unfold. The first lineup of the Seiyukai, Minseito, and Kokumin Domei factions is as follows: The Seiyukai will have Hamada Kunimatsu as the first to question general policy, followed by Okuchi Kiroku on financial issues, Uchida Shinya on national defense issues, Ashida Hitoshi on diplomatic issues, Kogure Butafu on economic issues, Tajiri Kazumin on current affairs issues, To Takeo on rural issues, and Miyazawa Yutaka on ideological issues. All are selected elites who will attack the government head-on. The Minseito will have Kawasaki Katsu raise financial issues as the vanguard, followed by Matsumoto Tadao on diplomatic issues and Nomura Karoku on ideological issues. The Kokumin Domei, from the standpoint of a purely opposition party, will have Nakano Seigo on diplomatic issues, Kiyose Ichiro on general politics, and Nonaka Tetsuya on exchange rate issues, launching a fierce attack. The questioners from the House of Peers have been decided as follows: on the essence of national politics and civil administration, Araki Yoshinori Count (Research Society); on financial, educational, and humanitarian issues, Ki Toshihide Baron (Kosei Society); on national defense issues, Mizuno Shigejiro; on financial, economic, and military affairs, Kato Masanosuke (Doseikai).

Adachi Attacks the Current Cabinet 78

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 20th: The Kokumin Domei held a general meeting of Diet members at its headquarters yesterday afternoon as a substitute for the party convention. President Adachi delivered a speech on the party's attitude towards the parliament as follows: The senile and incompetent current cabinet has intensified the anxieties of this extraordinary time and is daily creating the causes for a major collapse in the future. We [omission in original] hope for national unity, [omission in original] its own [omission in original] relaxed state, [omission in original] to rescue [omission in original] the trend [omission in original] against Japan's expectations. The debate in the League of Nations has degenerated into a formality, [omission in original] the essence of diplomacy is gradually moving towards direct action in the Far East. The recent anti-Japanese actions in China cannot be said to be unrelated to such an international atmosphere. We must have a resolute determination in the League of Nations debate and in essential diplomacy. The current cabinet's financial plan is [omission in original] separated and fractured. The feeling that the economy is improving is merely a delusion due to the depreciation of the exchange rate.

Seiyukai and Minseito Decide on Their Attitudes 79

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 20th: The parliament will reconvene tomorrow. The Seiyukai and Minseito each held party conventions today to clarify their attitudes towards the parliament to the world. The Seiyukai held a general meeting at its headquarters at 2:00 PM. President Suzuki and other officers and party members attended. President Suzuki was elected as chairman. After passing the declaration, the executive committee was elected. President Suzuki gave an encouraging speech. The Minseito held a general meeting at Seiyo-ken in Ueno at 1:00 PM. A declaration and resolution were passed, advocating four major policies: finance, currency, exchange rate, and industrial control. President Wakatsuki also delivered a speech on the party's attitude towards the parliament.

Summary of Wakatsuki's Speech 80

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 20th: The main points of President Wakatsuki's speech at the Minseito general meeting held at Seiyo-ken in Ueno at 1:00 PM this afternoon are as follows: 1. The discussions in the League of Nations by smaller countries are not something to be overjoyed or worried about. With an unwavering belief, we should aim to reach the true conclusion of the issue. 2. In the state of gold export prohibition, the easily fallen into evils are excessive currency inflation, which raises prices, threatens the lives of the people, disrupts creditor-debtor relations, and destroys the credit system, leading the financial world to collapse. This is what European countries experienced after the war. Therefore, the government and the people should be vigilant and not repeat this mistake. 3. The outline of the budget plan has already been published. There are huge expenditures, and the interest payments on public bonds still rely on the issuance of public bonds. This is, of course, an extraordinary abnormality in the financial plan and is deeply worrying. In the future, the interest on public bonds should be paid from permanent sources of revenue, seize the opportunity to achieve low interest rates, and attempt to swap to low-interest national bonds is necessary. 4. It is an urgent task at present to curb the fluctuations in the exchange rate and devise emergency measures to achieve moderate stability. 5. A part of the world blames the current economic turmoil on the economic structure. Although the current economic structure has some evils, its foundation is not wrong. Therefore, the state should guide and implement appropriate controls on production and sales. 6. The greatest worries of the nation and society today are the agitation of national thought and social unrest. Therefore, I firmly believe that rejecting dangerous thoughts, guiding wrong thoughts, and stabilizing people's hearts are urgent tasks today. Therefore, it is necessary to establish the authority of the parliament, and improvements should be made in the operation of the administration and the exercise of judicial power. 7. It is regrettable that there are those who deny constitutional politics, even if the scope is small. The so-called advocacy of dictatorship and oligarchy is theoretically, historically, and practically worthless.

Saito Granted an Audience with the Emperor 81

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 20th: Prime Minister Saito entered the palace at 1:00 PM today to grant an audience with the Emperor and reported in detail on the contents of the policy speech to be delivered in parliament. Afterwards, he withdrew. Finance Minister Takahashi and Foreign Minister Uchida also successively entered the palace to grant an audience and reported on their speeches in parliament.

Attitude Towards the Manchurian Dispute 82

▲ Reuters, Tokyo, 20th: The Minseito and Seiyukai will both publish resolutions on domestic and foreign policy when parliament opens this afternoon. The Minseito resolution states that Japan must adopt a firm attitude towards the Manchurian dispute in accordance with international justice, and the people should have a common and united front on this issue. The resolution states that Japan's attitude towards the Manchurian dispute is based on safeguarding peace in the Far East, which is recognized by members of the League of Nations. It also states that Japan's attitude towards the Manchurian issue will not change under any circumstances or under any external pressure. It hopes that the people will proceed calmly in this national crisis. The resolution also states the need to restore constitutionality as soon as possible.

Predictions on the Future of the Political Situation 83

▲ Reuters, Tokyo, 20th: The Japanese Diet will resume tomorrow after the New Year recess, which is attracting national attention. The Seiyukai and Minseito both held general meetings this afternoon, which were well attended, to decide on the party program for this session. Although only 33 parliamentarians openly oppose the government, it is generally expected that it will not be easy for the government to obtain large sums of money to balance its budget. The Seiyukai is the largest party in the Diet, but there are many party members who are prepared to strongly criticize the government, especially Finance Minister Takahashi, even though Takahashi is also a member of the Seiyukai and was once the president of the Seiyukai. However, the Seiyukai's attitude towards the Saito Cabinet is not consistent, [omission in original] which is a weakness on the opposition's side, because many people in the Seiyukai believe that the current period is a time of national crisis and it is not appropriate to have party strife. Public sentiment in Japan generally believes that the current Prime Minister is doing a reasonably good job in handling domestic and foreign affairs. The angry and frenzied image of a few months ago, which led to assassination attempts and other violent acts, seems to have largely dissipated. It is generally expected that such violent acts will not occur during the current Diet session. According to [omission in original] politicians' opinions, if Saito is [omission in original], then the political [omission in original] or may [omission in original], even [omission in original] the whole country, [omission in original] give extreme opposition parties and fanatics [omission in original] an opportunity. The Japanese people do not have much confidence in the Diet. At a time when the hardships of the people have not diminished, and the rural areas are particularly [omission in original] difficult, pushing [omission in original] the government and plunging the country into danger will [omission in original] make radical elements rampant. [omission in original] Prefecture still has the support of the people, or it will not fail. However, some people in the Seiyukai hope that the government can be reorganized without causing a major political upheaval and achieve a purely party cabinet. Future fierce battles will focus on the budget plan, which will be difficult for the government to defend. It is also expected that disturbances will occur in the House of Representatives, but the authorities have already considered special precautions to deal with such incidents.

Japan Prevents Domestic Reddening with Foreign Policy 84

National Defense Research Associations Established Throughout the Country

▲ Rengo Tsushin, Tokyo, 20th: Last year, more than 7,000 left-wing elements were arrested on suspicion of Reddening movements. The police authorities are extremely alarmed by the strong base of the Kigen and are especially focusing their efforts on the youth training programs of the Army Ministry, which attaches great importance to the Reddening of soldiers. The Army Ministry is determined to actively carry out a major mobilization on the ideological front. According to the Army Ministry's plan, National Defense Research Associations will be established in major cities in each prefecture and county throughout the country. These associations will transcend political parties and factions, promote the national spirit, guide thought, guide local young men and women, study national defense, and provide relief to wounded soldiers. The governors of each prefecture and county or powerful individuals will serve as guides.

Members will include students, young men and women's groups, police officers, veterans, merchants, industrialists, farmers, and all other classes. Currently, twenty prefectures and counties, including Kumamoto and Fukuoka, have already organized these associations. The Army Ministry plans to extend this movement to all universities and vocational schools throughout the country, with each school organizing a National Defense Research Association. Keio University in Tokyo will be the first to organize the Keio University National Defense Research Association at 1:00 PM on the 20th. It is reported that when these research associations are established throughout the country, the number of members will reach 20 million, which can prevent the intrusion of Reddening thought. The Army authorities are earnestly hoping for its future development.

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 20th: At today's regular cabinet meeting, the Japanese government discussed the Communist Party incident and the responsibility of Justice Minister Oyama in connection with it. As a result, it was decided that the government would actively explain the contents of the incident in parliament and request that a closed-door meeting be held in parliament on the 21st or 23rd.

World Economic Conference 85

Preparatory Committee Publishes Report

▲ Havas, Geneva, 19th: The preparatory committee for the World Economic Conference has completed the agenda for the conference tonight. The World Economic Conference, as decided by the League of Nations Executive Council, will be convened in London. The date of the convocation is yet to be determined. The organizing group is scheduled to meet on January 25th. The preparatory committee has prepared a general report for it. The committee explained the seriousness of the situation, the chaos of currency, the fall of prices, and the reduction of trade, but also pointed out considerable signs of improvement. The preparatory committee declared that the debts between governments, which have not been resolved for a long time, are an insurmountable obstacle to economic and financial recovery. Therefore, negotiations should be started and resolved as soon as possible. The preparatory committee also pointed out the main issues that countries should study: 1. Restore the real monetary standard between countries. 2. Use low-interest policies to facilitate the healthy development of various industries. 3. Supervising the surplus exchange rate is a key condition for the recovery of various industries. Governments should study the possibility of rapidly restoring the freedom of exchange rates and adopt strategies that can recirculate the capital that is currently stagnant. 4. Special commercial obstacles caused by economic panic should be abolished as soon as possible, that is, abolishing import quantity restrictions and easing tariff policies. The preparatory committee concluded in this part of its report, saying that efforts towards commercial freedom are directly related to stable currency. To maintain an international monetary system without basing it on an international economic system is impossible.

▲ Reuters, London, 19th: The report of the Preparatory Committee for the World Economic Conference, published today, advocates that the governments of the world should immediately start working to restore the normal exchange of goods. Countries should do their best to find a universal agreement to gradually release temporary emergency plans implemented during trade panic, such as banning imports and restricting import quotas, in order to finally completely abolish them. The World Economic Conference may not be able to convene until May at the earliest. Although the silver issue is included in the agenda, this report does not pay attention to the position of silver in the world currency system. The report believes that any behavior that raises prices and gold prices can benefit silver and other low-priced goods.

▲ Reuters, Paris, 19th: French President Lebrun informed the government that he is willing to reduce his salary by [omission in original] percent. The House Finance Committee today voted 24 to 11 to consider the budget plan proposed by the Socialist Party and to base its discussion on the government's plan. The result of this move seems to be a major change to the government's proposal, because the government's proposal is very unpopular and has harmed the position of the Pongouin cabinet.

Sichuan's Two Lius Suddenly Cooperate Again 88

Since the Jing Conference Implemented a Truce

Both Sides, Exhausted, Know Retreating is Difficult

The Battle of Chengdu is About to Reignite

According to Chongqing dispatches, following the conclusion of the Neijiang Conference, many rumors have arisen in Sichuan. The most noteworthy is the news that Liu Wenhui has turned his guns around to counterattack Deng and Tian's forces. Because Liu's counterattack on Rongwei failed and resulted in heavy losses, he sought another way out, first seeking peace with the 21st Army, expressing his willingness to unconditionally cease the great war in southern Sichuan, and requesting Liu Xiang not to press him further. He prepared to reorganize his forces and strike out towards Xinjin, Shuangliu, Renshou, and Meishan, to seize the territory of the 28th and 29th Armies. Thus, the voices of cooperation between the two Lius spread like thunder for a time.

Conditions for Cooperation Between the Two Lius: The cooperation between the two Lius was initiated by generals Leng Zhendong, Tian Boshi, and Du Shaoshang of the 24th Army, who went to Zijing to meet with Liu Xiang and discuss cooperation methods. After repeated consultations, it is said that four cooperation measures were agreed upon: (1) The 21st and 24th Armies should cease fire immediately; (2) The 24th Army should not interfere with the 21st Army's occupation of the 24th Army's defense zone; (3) The 21st Army should not assist in any attacks on any part of the Allied forces by the 24th Army; (4) The 24th Army should not launch any further counterattacks against the 21st Army. Liu Xiang, considering that the four measures were of little significance, agreed to sign them. He believed that since his army had set out, the benefits he had gained were better than those of other armies. Although the 24th Army had been defeated, its vitality had not yet been lost. If they only knew to fight to the death, it would be impossible to predict who would win. It would be better to take advantage of the victory and withdraw, doing a favor to the 24th Army by agreeing to their request. After the truce conference between the two sides was completed, Liu Xiang returned to Chongqing from the Zijing headquarters on the 12th. The areas of Jiading, Jingyan, and Renshou counties were then designated as buffer zones. Both sides still left a small number of troops to guard the front line, each fifty miles apart, with the rest moving to the rear.

Liu Wenhui's Army Returns to Chengdu: Liu Wenhui of the 24th Army collected the remaining troops and reorganized them into ten mixed brigades, each brigade stipulated to have 10,000 men. The insufficient numbers were to be expanded within a limited time. However, Liu, being situated in a corner of upper southern Sichuan, half of which was a barren and impoverished area, found the army's pay to be quite a problem. Liu privately planned to station the troops in Yaan, Ningyuan, and western Kangding, to nurture their strength and await the opportunity to stage a comeback. However, as the end of the old year approached and the weather turned cold, the borderlands were covered with snow, and everything above Yaan became another world. The soldiers of this unit, whose daily lives had been more comfortable than those of other units, suddenly heard of being moved to the borderlands, where they would suffer from hunger and cold in the icy and snowy conditions. Therefore, before the order was even issued, they had already risen in opposition. Liu had no choice but to convene a military conference of all officers in Meishan to discuss the army's future. The subordinate generals all believed that the province's revenue was quite extensive, and that the unconditional surrender to the 28th and 29th Armies last time was only to maintain the status quo. Now that they had signed non-aggression treaties with the 20th Army, there was no need to worry about the rear. They should return to the province and take over all the institutions, and since Deng and Tian's forces were weak, they dared not resist. Otherwise, they should use all their strength to eliminate the 28th and 29th Armies to vent their anger over the defeat. Liu agreed and led his troops back to the province, issuing a telegram from Meishan announcing his return to the province, saying: "Since Sichuan lost control, wars have been frequent, and soldiers have never had a peaceful year. What crime have the people of Sichuan committed, suffering repeatedly from military disasters? The thought of the children left behind burns in my heart. This sudden outbreak of flames spread like wildfire, and urgent dispatches flew back and forth, causing national uproar. Day and night, I feel deeply guilty. Wenhui, as a soldier, has always been wary of resorting to military force and has worked hard to maintain peace from beginning to end. In the early stages of the brewing war, I suffered immense pain and repeatedly made concessions, hoping to avoid disputes. This sincere intention has been seen by all. After all, the chaos in Sichuan cannot be resolved by military force. To seek the root cause and purify the source, the first step is to govern according to law. If chaos is used to replace chaos, if something is taken or lost, the tangled threads will become more chaotic, and seeking the source will only exhaust it. Then the long night will have no end. This intention has already been presented in detail to the central government and conveyed to the elders in the province, and there is no need to repeat it. I hope it is understood. I am also grateful to the elders of the province, as well as the institutions and organizations, for running around and shouting at the top of their lungs, hoping to eliminate the chaos and achieve peace. Who knew that their good intentions would not be understood, and the more they tried to be patient, the more they were invaded. Defensive action was truly unavoidable. The battle of Chengdu, with fierce fighting for days, frustrated their power and was unavoidable. The elders and brothers were again subjected to the suffering of war. Thinking back to the past, there is still pain. The battle of Rongwei lasted for more than ten days, with blood shed on the battlefield and countless casualties. The loss of military supplies was even more immeasurable. In addition, the people, already exhausted, suffered the burden of heavy supplies, and the devastation was heartbreaking. If this continues, how will it end? Therefore, we temporarily resolved to cease fire, restore peace, and jointly plan for the aftermath, using the available military strength to save the nation's foundation, which is on the verge of collapse. I hope to live up to my private intentions and give the people a chance to rest, dispel the clouds, and see the light. This is what all the elders and brothers in Sichuan have been longing for. Wenhui, having mistakenly assumed the provincial government during a time of many troubles, felt responsible for suppressing the chaos. He left the province to supervise the army, and the military life was hurried. Now that the war has subsided and everything is waiting to be rebuilt, I plan to return to Chengdu to discuss governance. However, I have heard rumors that the provincial capital is still in turmoil. Since I released the prisoners first, would they repay kindness with revenge? They have not lost their conscience, and I don't think they would do such a thing. If, because Wenhui left the province, they occupied my military and government institutions, burned my officers' residences, massacred my wounded soldiers, and robbed my personnel left in the province, they are uneasy and fear revenge. So they pretend to be virtuous and cause alarm. However, Wenhui, as a soldier, would never resort to violence to replace violence, indulging in barbarism. I have strictly ordered my subordinates not to violate them in the slightest. If anyone deliberately violates this order, they will be killed immediately. If they think that everyone is easy to deal with, are brave and call themselves soldiers, and do not care about harming the local area and burdening my elders and brothers, Wenhui has no choice but to deal with them temporarily in order to maintain the overall situation. I feel that my talent is inadequate to meet the heavy responsibilities and cannot prevent problems before they arise, nor can I stop the war once it has started. I have failed to live up to the central government's trust and the people's expectations. Thinking about this at midnight, I am saddened and tears stream down my face. Looking forward, I am filled with many feelings. I plan to return to my post soon to pacify the people. Peace and governance depend on renewal. I hope that all the elders and brothers in Sichuan will come forward to teach me. Liu Wenhui bows."

Five Elders and Seven Worthies Mediate: After Liu's telegram was issued, the people in Chengdu were panic-stricken, startled several times a night, thinking that the great war was about to resume and that the people would suffer the hardship of war again. At the same time, Liu Wenhui's advance troops had moved to the front lines of Xinjin and Shuangliu, only forty miles from Chengdu. Liu Wenhui himself had also arrived in Xinjin, and the situation was extremely serious. Deng Xihou and Tian Songyao were even more panicked. In addition to the two armies deploying heavy troops to Qinglongchang, Shiyangchang, and Hongpailou (all more than ten miles from Chengdu) to prevent Liu's army from returning to the province, the Five Elders and Seven Worthies of Chengdu (respected elders from all over Sichuan) came forward to mediate, hoping to avoid the resumption of war. But what the future holds is still unknown. (January 16)

Qingdao is the Main Hub for the Import of Japanese Goods

Daily Transactions Exceed 10 Million Yuan 89

＝Total Imports Have Increased Several Times Over＝

＝Nine Chinese Merchants Cooperating with Japanese Merchants＝

Qingdao Dispatch: Since the September 18th Incident, the entire country has been filled with righteous indignation. However, Qingdao alone remains as peaceful and prosperous as ever, and unscrupulous merchants are even more eager to sell Japanese goods, resulting in the market being flooded with them. According to news from the docks, the total amount of Japanese goods imported through Qingdao recently has increased several times compared to before September 18th. Qingdao has become the main hub for the import of Japanese goods, and even representatives from Shaanxi, Gansu, Yunnan, and Guizhou provinces have been sent to Qingdao to order Japanese goods, which is extremely hateful. What is even more hateful is that the Chinese merchants in the exchange (the exchange is nominally a Sino-Japanese joint venture but is actually monopolized by Japanese merchants), who were previously pressured by the Japanese and withdrew from the exchange, organized a Qingdao Municipal Exchange in the Qiyan Guild Hall, dealing in all kinds of silver, money, and goods transactions. Recently, nine unscrupulous merchants, including Fu Judong, have vigorously advocated Sino-Japanese cooperation and resumed business in the exchange on the 14th of this month in order to carry out their pro-foreign behavior. It is said that when Fu Judong and other merchants returned to the exchange to start trading, they first held a meeting at the money and goods exchange, chaired by Ando, the Japanese director, who reported on the process of the Chinese merchants' return to the exchange and stated the rules to be followed in the market thereafter, finally expressing his welcome. Next, Liu Shuheng, the manager of the Chinese merchant Lifenghao, spoke about the benefits of the Chinese merchants returning to the exchange and urged everyone to abide by the rules, conspire for mutual benefit, and not be impulsive or violate the regulations. Anyone who disrupts the market will be punished accordingly. Finally, he wished that Sino-Japanese traders would trade together forever without separation. It is also heard that the Chinese merchants who returned to the exchange this time have extravagant desires and are preparing to complete transactions of more than 10 million yuan with the Japanese side every day. Seeing this situation, the Japanese merchants have hired Wang Weibin, the manager of Xieyuansheng, and Liu Shuheng, the manager of Lifenghao, as consultants to strive to develop the exchange's business. Songjiang: Songxing Distributes Debentures

After the collapse of Songjiang Bank, Qu Yuehua, the lawyer for the bondholders' representative, is in the process of pursuing litigation. Another group of bondholders, represented by Chen Nianci and Mo Wenxiong, through their lawyers Peng Zhongjun and Gu Shouyi, submitted a petition to President Wang of the County Court, stating that it is now the cold end of the year and the Spring Festival requires funds. The bondholders in this group are all small overseas households who are relatively poor. They requested the County Court to be considerate and immediately distribute the funds for their use, and suggested that bondholders with claims of less than 100 yuan should be paid in full, those with claims of less than 200 yuan should be paid 60%, and those with claims of less than 500 yuan should be paid 40%. After the petition was sent to the liquidation office for review and reply, the office has now decided to distribute half a percentage to all bondholders from the funds received from the litigation, with a remaining 2,000 yuan. In addition, 4,000 yuan was returned by the rubber factory to be distributed among the smaller bondholders to show consideration. It is calculated that those with claims of 50 yuan or less will be paid in full, those with claims of less than 100 yuan will be paid 30%, and those with claims of less than 200 yuan will be paid 15%. The payment period will be from the 21st of this month to the 10th of February, and President Wang has issued a public notice to inform everyone.

Major Fire in the City Late at Night 90

At the home of a Mr. Zhao at the intersection of Xianqian Street and Zhongxin Street last night (the 19th) at three o'clock, a customer of a vendor selling *tanfen* left embers behind, which ignited rice straw. Soon, the fire alarm rang wildly, and fire trucks and police arrived at the scene one after another, doing their best to put out the fire. Duan Qirui's Reply to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 98

Why Should There Be Any Difference Between the Court and the Opposition in Defending Against Aggression?

In the Past, Force Could Not Subdue Me

How Could Humble Words Tempt Me?

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Local Association, and other organizations recently learned that the Japanese side was greatly enticing both the Duan and Wu factions, falsely claiming that the people should join hands, and trying their best to win them over, releasing an atmosphere of peace to confuse people. They telegraphed Tianjin Duan Zhiqian and Beiping Wu Ziyu, requesting them to refuse to meet with the Japanese and to state their attitude and restrain their old subordinates, not to fall into the trap. After the telegrams were sent, it was discovered that Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, had received a reply telegram from Duan, clearly expressing his attitude towards resisting aggression. The two telegrams are recorded below:

Telegram from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: To Mr. Duan Zhiqian and Mr. Wu Ziyu of Tianjin and Beiping: The Japanese warlords are determined to use the strategy of "using Chinese to destroy Chinese", secretly instigating frustrated military and political figures to be their pawns, and using a small number of troops as their support, hoping to take control of the whole country without bloodshed, trying it in the Northeast and succeeding. Now it is said that they will try it again in North China. The enemy is not to be blamed, what is worrying is that there are still people like Ding Shiyuan in our country for them to use. How can the mistake of Wu Sangui be repeated? Moreover, the Japanese policy of using traitors is more brutal than that of the Qing Dynasty. How can there be a good ending? The generals in the Northeast are still able to escape the cage and not be tempted. Your prestige and history are above them, and you have many old subordinates. Although you are full of righteousness, the Japanese will never forget you. Humble words and generous gifts, and nightly advances, are a matter of fact. I implore you to deal with them with the righteousness of Yan Changshan and Wen Tianxiang, so that their conspiracy can be foiled, and warn your old subordinates not to be used. This spiritual confrontation is ten times more effective than beheading generals and seizing flags. In the past, Gongshan did not comply with the rebels, and he still knew that a gentleman should not besiege his country, let alone you, Ming Gong. I beseech you to issue a declaration quickly, so as to stabilize the people's will. Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, bows.

Duan Zhiqian's Reply Telegram: To Chairman Wang of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and forwarded to the Shanghai Municipal Local Association and the Exchange Association: Both telegrams have been read. I am saddened by the national crisis and honored to be encouraged by righteousness. I am determined to dedicate myself to the country and will not lag behind others. Other things should not be mentioned for the time being. In the past, when the whole country was mad about the monarchy, I was still upright and outspoken. Force could not subdue me, how could humble words tempt me? Why should there be any difference between the court and the opposition in defending against aggression? It is my duty and there is no need to promote it. There are many people of insight on the sea who are knowledgeable. Know that eloquence is not as good as facts. Duan Qirui, printed seal.

The Righteous Army Relief Society Appeals for Aid for Li and Deng 100

Battalions Retreating from Rehe under Ma and Feng

Allocation of Military Supplies and Trucks

The Shanghai Northeast Volunteer Army Relief Society issued four official letters yesterday, all of which are extremely important. They are recorded separately as follows:

Appealing for Aid for Li and Deng: The Society previously received telegrams from Ma Zhanshan and Li Zhongyi requesting assistance. After discussion, it was decided to allocate existing funds for ammunition and cotton clothing to provide practical assistance, and to send letters to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Northeast Refugee Relief Society to request relief. This was previously reported in the newspaper. Based on the resolution, the Society sent separate letters to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Northeast Refugee Relief Society yesterday stating: Respectfully, We received a telegram from General Zhu Ziqiao stating that Li Zhongyi, the General Commander of the 8th Army Corps of the Righteous Army, due to Ma Zhanshan's departure and the exhaustion of ammunition and aid, had no choice but to select 27,000 elite cavalry and infantry troops and arrive at [blank space], but had no way to raise funds for the men and horses. With limited strength, they had to telegraph requesting prompt relief to show consolation, etc. We also received a genuine telegram from General Wan Fulin through Mr. Wu Huanzhang, the representative of Chairman Ma Zhanshan (as seen in yesterday's telegram), etc. After combining these and discussing them, as the funds donated and stored by our Society are not large, it was decided that in addition to our Society allocating 300,000 rounds of ammunition for the 7.9mm rifle, a relief fund of 10,000 yuan, and 2,000 pieces of cotton blankets and clothing to the various armies retreating from Rehe in Heilongjiang, we would also request your Society and the Northeast Refugee Relief Society (your Society and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce) to find other ways to provide relief. Therefore, we respectfully request that your Society, mindful of the hardships and tribulations suffered by the Li and Deng troops for over a year, grant them relief so that we can achieve the effect of many hands making light work. We sincerely hope you will investigate and handle this matter, and we are deeply grateful.

Providing Relief to Lao Bei Feng: The Society sent a letter to Mr. Yang Wenfei, the representative of Zhang Haitian (i.e., Lao Bei Feng), stating: Respectfully, It has been resolved at the 98th meeting of our Standing Committee to allocate 100,000 rounds of ammunition for the 7.9mm rifle and a relief fund of 5,000 yuan to the Lao Bei Feng troops, which will be remitted to General Zhu Ziqiao for transfer. We are sending this letter to inform you. Please check and report to your Commander to prepare receipts and receive them from General Zhu for use. Sincerely, to Mr. Yang Wenlong, Representative of Commander Zhang Haitian of the 3rd Corps of the 2nd Army Corps of the Northeast Volunteer Army.

Allocating Cotton Clothing to Zhou Han: The Society sent a letter to Zhou Han, Commander of the 3rd Route Cavalry of the Northeast Anti-Japanese National Salvation Volunteer Army, stating: Respectfully, We received your letter of January 17 stating that you were previously granted cotton blankets and clothing by your Society, which has been communicated to the front lines, and the entire army is overjoyed, requesting prompt allocation so that they can return north as soon as possible, etc. We have approved this. It has been resolved at the 98th meeting of our Standing Committee to allocate 200 sets of cotton clothing. We are sending this letter to inform you. Please check and prepare receipts to collect them from the Society and transport them to the front lines for distribution.

Assisting with Military Trucks: The Society previously received letters from Jiang Songnian and Wu Huanzhang, representatives of Ma Zhanshan, and Pang Yuedong, representative of Feng Zhanhai, requesting assistance in donating trucks to facilitate military transportation, etc. The Society sent a special reply yesterday stating: Respectfully, We received your letter of January 15 stating that the Ma and Feng troops are retreating to the border of Rehe, and transportation is extremely difficult. Please allocate some of the military trucks that our Society has raised funds to purchase to facilitate military operations, etc. We have approved this. According to our Society's previous allocation of 80,000 yuan to purchase one million rounds of ammunition, as the order was inconvenient, we telegraphed General Zhu to request the Ministry of Military Affairs to claim them on our behalf, and then used the funds to purchase military trucks and send them to General Zhu for use. Now that we have received the previous request, it has been resolved to telegraph General Zhu to request a discretionary allocation for use. We sent a telegram to General Zhu on the 19th of this month requesting the allocation, and the original telegram is recorded on a separate sheet for your reference. Sincerely, we hope you will investigate this matter. We also sent a telegram to General Zhu Ziqiao stating: Recently, Pang Quanfeng, representative of Feng Zhanhai, and Wu Huanzhang and Jiang Songnian, representatives of Ma Zhanshan, came to the Society and stated that the Feng and Ma troops, who are currently stationed in the northern part of Rehe, number over 50,000, and transportation is extremely difficult. Please allocate several trucks from your Society to assist with military transportation, etc. As the Feng and Ma troops have now become the main force of the Righteous Army, it seems that they should be given all kinds of convenience. Please allocate the military trucks purchased and sent to your office by our Society to the Feng and Ma troops within a possible scope to facilitate transportation to the front lines. We are deeply grateful.

Telegram from the Second Army Commander of Heilongjiang Province Reporting Temporary Retreat to Linxi 101

Complete Lack of All Replacements

Wu Huanzhang, representative of General Ma Zhanshan stationed in Shanghai, and Jiang Songnian, Councilor of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government, received a telegram from Mr. Shao Binshan, Commander of the Second Army of Heilongjiang Province, which stated: (Omitted above) I have received your kind telegram. I am very ashamed of your encouragement. I was saddened by our parting last autumn, separated by the clouds. This time, our army abandoned the river and retreated to Rehe, which is not only heartbreaking for the commander-in-chief, but also for every soldier. However, due to the exhaustion of ammunition and aid, and the lack of food and supplies, the commander-in-chief, considering that the decline was irreversible, ordered the various armies to retreat and await orders in order to preserve their strength for another battle. My brothers and I took the path through the Solun Mountains, traveling for more than a month. During this severe winter, food was insufficient, and more than 400 people died of hunger and cold. When we approached Manzhan, the enemy blocked the dangerous passes and attacked, and armored vehicles pursued us. After two days and nights of fierce fighting, although we killed hundreds of enemies and captured six armored vehicles, more than 700 of our officers and soldiers were killed in battle. The casualties were heavy, and the officers and soldiers were all indignant and wanted to fight to eliminate the enemy. However, due to hunger and exhaustion, and the exhaustion of ammunition, what good would it do to fight with bare hands? Moreover, several thousand brave men had been through many bloody battles, and we could not bear to lightly sacrifice the elite troops in the army, so we temporarily retreated to Linxi to await reinforcements and hope to fight again. I have been traveling arduously, and the men are tired and the horses are weak, and our clothes are torn and our shoes are worn out. Although the local government has temporarily provided supplies so that we are not starving, all replacements are lacking. I hope you will do your best to help. This is what I look forward to. Your brother Shao Binshan respectfully bows.

Zhang Qun Discusses the Policy for Handling Sichuan Affairs 103

Intends to Engage in Sincere Consultation Before Entering Sichuan

To Seek a Common Solution

According to the Central News Agency, the Central Political Conference recently decided to specially appoint Central Committee Member Zhang Yuejun to Sichuan to discuss concrete measures for reorganizing Sichuan affairs with the Sichuan provincial authorities, based on the 17th-year National Government order. After receiving the order, Mr. Zhang has been in Shanghai for several days, engaging in preliminary consultations with representatives of various generals, including Liu Xiang, Liu Wenhui, and Tian Songyao. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Zhang at his residence yesterday afternoon and asked about the date of his trip to Sichuan and the policy for handling Sichuan affairs. According to Mr. Zhang, the recent turmoil in Sichuan is particularly regrettable at a time when the country is in serious difficulty. The central government is concerned about the overall situation and concerned about the western frontier. The 340th meeting of the Central Political Conference decided to send me to Sichuan to discuss specific implementation measures with the Sichuan provincial authorities based on the central government order of the 17th year. I believe that the safety of Sichuan is related to the overall situation, and the central government must want me to return to Sichuan to discuss matters, so I can only reluctantly make a trip to show my respect and reverence to my hometown, which is also my great wish. However, the disputes in Sichuan have been going on for a long time, and the situation is extremely complex, making a solution very difficult. Recently, the generals in Sichuan, mindful of the difficulties of the times, have stopped internal strife. Taking advantage of this opportunity, if we can jointly seek a solution, end the past, and start a new chapter, so that the people of Sichuan will not suffer the pain of fire and water again, it will be a blessing for Sichuan and a fortune for the country. As for the method of discussing Sichuan affairs, we should of course proceed based on the central government order of the 17th year. However, the road to Sichuan is far away, and it takes time to travel back and forth. At this time, the country is facing many difficulties and there are many things to discuss, so it is difficult to leave for a long time. In order to shorten the time spent in Sichuan, I plan to engage in sincere consultations with the central government's relevant departments and ministries, as well as the Sichuan authorities, in the spirit of impartiality and selflessness, before entering Sichuan. Once there is a slight clue, I will start the journey, and the time spent in Sichuan is expected to be enough to complete the work in one month. As for the establishment of the Sichuan Political Reorganization Committee, the central government is still considering it.

Various Trade Associations Request the Abolition of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement 105

Advocating the Use of Tariff Policies for National Products

Commerce and Politics Should No Longer Be Extended

The various trade associations in this city held a joint meeting at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon to discuss the expiration of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement and the matter of not accepting further negotiations. A total of more than 80 trade associations, including the cotton cloth industry, silk industry, spinning industry, sugar industry, color printing industry, north-south goods exchange industry, new medicine industry, wool industry, rice industry, coal ash industry, and mercerized cotton textile industry, attended, with more than 90 people including Luo Qinghua, Zheng Chengqing, Lu Fengzhu, Chen Songyuan, Lu Wenshao, Zhu Wenqi, Ma Shaoquan, Xie Zhongle, Zheng Zenan, Tu Kaizheng, Ge Jieshen, Ke Ganchen, Ye Jiaxing, and Jin Runxiang. Luo Qinghua chaired the meeting and resolved the following cases: (1) Jointly petition the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry to declare the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement invalid and not to be renewed upon expiration. (2) Petition the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to send telegrams to chambers of commerce across the country to advocate for unity. (3) Appoint representatives to petition in Nanjing, to be appointed at the next joint meeting. (4) Submit a document to Zheng Chengqing to be responsible for drafting. The meeting adjourned after the discussion. The following is the document from the various trade associations to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Ministry of Finance: Presenting a petition. It is found that the tariff reciprocity agreement between our country and Japan in the 19th year of the Republic of China will expire on May 6 of this year. General opinion believes that it should not be renewed. In terms of commercial interests, textile factories, flour mills, and marine products are either the main industries of our country or related to the livelihood of coastal fishermen. Japan is geographically close, and the above three items have abundant production and low prices. If taxes are levied at the current lowest tax rate, they will be imported continuously, becoming more prosperous year by year. The operation of factories and the livelihood of fishermen will be taken away and there will be no way to survive. The original meaning of our country's efforts to achieve tariff autonomy was to use tariff policies to maintain infant industries, not just to increase tax revenue. If industries related to the livelihood of the people are not considered for maintenance, then what is the point of tariff autonomy and advocating for national products? The government's advocacy of national products is different from that of ordinary people. It is not just a matter of issuing a notice, but of personally practicing it. The most effective method is to use tariff policies so that our country's products do not suffer extreme pressure. When China and Japan negotiated reciprocal tariffs, the Japanese initially intended to set the effective period to ten or seven years, but our side only allowed three years. This approach was only temporary and transitional. The reason why the deadline was shortened at the time is sufficient to justify why it should not be extended again today. Some argue that if reciprocity expires, the commerce of overseas Chinese will plummet. It is not known that this is precisely what the Japanese are using as bait. For example, silk fabrics are only taxed at 30% less, with an actual tax of 70%, while at the same time, the Japanese are encouraging Japanese in silk and hemp producing areas to manufacture and sell locally in Korea. Korean merchants have long been oppressed to the point of no return. As for instigating riots and driving people back to their home countries, it goes without saying. Under these circumstances, what reciprocity is there to speak of? How can we pursue false fame and forget real disasters? In terms of political interests, the Japanese drive out our officials, kill our people, and occupy our land, and they are still encroaching on it. If this kind of situation happened in other countries, even if they did not resort to war, they would have already withdrawn their ambassadors and closed their markets. We still maintain a normal state and allow them to trade with all countries on the same basis as other countries, which is already a good way to maintain peace. Diplomatic operations should be used to check and balance each other. The way to control one matter with another and to control a third matter with the second is the proper strategy. If the Japanese do not return our invaded land, then we will refuse to negotiate the extension of reciprocity. This is a matter of course that can be announced to the world. Knowing that the Japanese will not hesitate to fight for the Eastern Provinces, this may not change their intention. However, leaving this as a check will still cause inconvenience to their commerce. Otherwise, they will first plunder our territory, and then we will grant them commercial benefits. For them, this is a two-pronged approach, while for us, it is tantamount to rewarding their labor of slaughter. If Chinese and foreign intellectuals see this, they will not only criticize us for being crazy and losing our minds, but also criticize us for willingly flattering the enemy, which will only increase the enemy's arrogance and help their aggression, which is not a blessing for the country. Based on the above reasons, the Sino-Japanese tariff reciprocity agreement should not be renewed upon expiration. Without waiting another day, we should submit a document to your government and departments for review and approval, and immediately declare that the aforementioned agreement will not be accepted for any further negotiations after expiration in order to maintain industry and show determination. This is a public envoy. Respectfully submitted, Shanghai Cotton Cloth Industry, Sugar Industry, Color Printing Industry, Rice Industry, Silk Industry, Sausage Industry, Spinning Industry, New Medicine Industry, Coal Ash Industry, Mercerized Cotton Textile Industry, North-South Goods Industry, Wool Industry, and more than 100 other trade associations.

Divided into Seven Groups, namely (1) Science Group, Yang Xingfo, Hu Gangfu, Song Wusheng, Ding Xielin, Wang Yunwu, (2) Agriculture Group, Xu Tinghu, Tan Xihong, Zou Bingwen, He Shangping, Zhu Fancun, Zhu Jube, Wu Huanru, Tang Qiyu, Wu Juenong, (3) Industry Group, Xu Peihuang, Cao Liangxia, Wang Shiqiang, Zhu Qiaoyi, Shi Boan, Xiang Kangyuan, Wu Yun Chu, Xue Cixin, Zhu Xianhang, Xu Shanxiang, Xi Cunge, Liu Yin Fu, Zhou Zijing, (4) Art Group, Ye Yuhu, Wang Yiting, Xia Jingguan, Wu Tianweng, Lang Jingshan, Jiang Xiaoji, Lin Fengmian, Liu Yazi, Xu Beihong, Liu Haisu, (5) Drama Group, Song Chunfang, Xu Muyun, Qi Rushan, Xu Liangchen, Zheng Jinwen, Chen Shutong, Ma Youwei, (6) Sports Group, Chu Minyi, Wang Zhengting, Zhang Zhijiang, Xu Zhendong, Zhu Shaoping, (7) Famous People's Achievements (Undetermined)

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Reorganizes Business and Recovers Hunan Provincial Shipping 109

The Hunan route of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was recently increased, and the docks and warehouses were all rented from the Pujii Company. Recently, the American Jiangjiang Company, in order to develop the shipping business on the Yangtze River, decided to increase the number of ships on the Hunan route, considering that Hunan rice is exported in large quantities. Because there were no docks or warehouses, Xu Zuxin was sent to Changsha to take over the Pujii docks, and a contract has been signed. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received the news and believed that this move involved the shipping rights of Hunan Province. If it fell into the hands of foreign merchants, it would stop the company's shipping business in Hunan. Therefore, it telegraphed the Hunan branch to strongly request the Pujii Company to revoke the foreign merchant's contract and continue to lease it to the company. Yesterday, it received a telegram stating that this matter had been successfully completed, and the shipping rights of Hunan Province had been recovered. The renewal contract is being signed.

Stopping the Guangli Steamboat: The Guangli steamboat of the Nanyang line is over 40 years old, uses a lot of coal, and has a small speed. It has passed its production period. Liu Hongsheng specially ordered the chief captain and chief engineer to survey the ship's hull to see if it was suitable for use. As a result, due to excessive consumption and operating losses, it was decided to stop the ship and not sail it. Yesterday, it was towed to the Longhua River and anchored. All the business personnel and stewards in the ship were dismissed. Except for six people who were kept to look after the ship, all the rest, including the captain and the stoker, were laid off. Each was paid two months' salary and dismissed.

Insurance for Ship Staff and Seamen: The company has a total of 25 ships on the Yangtze River and the sea, with more than a thousand ship staff and seamen. In the past, when accidents occurred on the Xinhua and other ships, major disputes arose over the compensation for ship staff and seamen. Now, the shipping department has formulated a plan for all ship staff and seamen to uniformly insure against maritime accidents. The premium is very low and is deducted from the monthly salary. In the event of misfortune, compensation can be obtained to support their families. The plan has been approved and implemented by the general manager.

Continuing to Lease Inland River Ships: After the Zhejiang Construction Department leased the company's inland river ships, it subleased them to Zhang Jingpei for operation. This year, the lease is about to expire. The Zhejiang Construction Department specially sent a commissioner to Shanghai to discuss the renewal of the lease with General Manager Liu. Liu has agreed that the Zhejiang Construction Department will still have the priority to renew the lease when it expires.

New Ningxing Ship Refloated After Running Aground

The new Ningxing, a Yangtze River ship of the Sanbei Company, was carrying a large number of goods and passengers from Shanghai to Hankou this time. On the afternoon of the 18th, the ship ran aground on a shoal off the coast of Xiaogushan on the Zhenjiang River due to heavy snow. At that time, because the iron keel was too heavy, it sank into the shoal and could not move. The shipowner sent a telegram for help, which was received by the Changxing, a Yangtze River ship of our company, which sailed to tow it. After five hours of towing, it was still unable to pull it out of the shoal. The new Ningxing then sent a telegram to Shanghai for help. The Shanghai office telegraphed the Fengpu ship to sail to assist in the towing. It was not until yesterday morning that a telegram was received stating that the new Ningxing had been pulled out of the shoal by the combined efforts of the Changxing and Fengpu. It is not yet known whether the hull was damaged and must be inspected after unloading the goods in Hankou.

Wusong Ship Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 110

The Wusong steamboat sailed back to Shanghai from Hankou at 2 pm yesterday and docked at the Taikoo Wharf. After receiving a telegram from Hankou in advance, the company was deeply afraid of accidents at the wharf and specially requested the French Concession Police to send detectives to protect it in case of emergency. Therefore, around 1 pm yesterday, more than 30 Chinese and Western detectives, armed with live ammunition, were closely guarding the vicinity of the wharf, and traffic was almost cut off. Suspicious pedestrians were also inspected. They had not retreated by the evening, so all the stewards on the ship could not board the ship to work.
